The Moral and Philosophical Critique of Independent Human Agency
Nasafi presents moral and philosophical arguments against Mu'tazili independence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the moral argument that human acts cannot be independently created by God without attributing evil to Him, and the philosophical refutation of a 'meaning beyond existence' as the basis of agency.

Core Idea
Direct creation of evil acts by God is more blameworthy than committing them, and a 'meaning' beyond existence is unintelligible.

Having established the logical impossibility of independent human power, Imam Nasafi now turns to moral and philosophical considerations. He argues that if God were to directly produce evil human acts, that would be worse than humans committing them directly. Furthermore, he dismisses the Mu'tazili claim that there is an additional ontological 'meaning' that makes an essence an agent, calling it contrary to reason. Let us examine these arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the moral argument
Identify the claim that human acts include ugly/foolish and the reasoning about production vs. direct agency.
Notice the term 'mubashara' and 'ijad'.
2
Examine the philosophical refutation
Understand why the claim of a 'meaning beyond existence' is rejected as unintelligible.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider how these arguments together refute the Mu'tazili position.
The author says these are their well-known doubts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the explanation of this: that Allah Most High, when He wills to bring about the act of the servant, the matter is either that the servant has the power of abstention or not. ?

?

?
The Mu'tazilites insisted on human independence to protect God from being associated with evil. In your own heart, do you ever try to distance God from your failures, subtly claiming some 'independence' from His control? What would it mean for you to fully accept that all acts—good and bad—occur by His creation and will?

The Proof from General Verse and the Mu'tazili Objection
Nasafi presents a proof and an objection from the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic proof that God is the creator of all things, including human acts, and the Mu'tazili objection that human acts must be excluded to preserve the verse's praise.

Core Idea
The general verse includes all things, but the Mu'tazila argue evil acts would undermine praise.

Imam Nasafi begins by presenting the central proof for the Maturidi doctrine of divine creation: the Quranic verse 'Creator of everything.' Since human acts are things, God must create them. He then introduces the Mu'tazili objection, which argues that including evil human acts contradicts the verse's purpose of praising God. This passage sets up a classic kalam debate between scriptural generality and rational purpose.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof from the general verse
Read the first part of the passage where Imam Nasafi states that the verse 'خَلِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ' (Creator of everything) proves God creates all things, including human acts, by its generality.
Notice that the proof is direct: human acts are things, so they fall under 'everything'.
2
Read the Mu'tazili objection
Read the second part where the opponents argue that human acts are excluded because the verse is praise, and including evil acts would turn it into blame.
Pay attention to the specific examples of evil acts they list.
3
Reflect on the missing response
The passage cuts off before Imam Nasafi's response. Think about how a Maturidi might refute this objection using other principles, such as the distinction between creating and commanding, or the nature of acquisition (kash).
This is an opportunity to engage with the broader kalam discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحجة لأهل الحق قوله تعالى : ( خَلِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ ) وأفعال العباد أشياء فيكون الله تعالى خالقها لعموم الآية، والخصوم يعترضون على ذلك فيقولون: أفعال العباد مخصوصة من هذه الآية بدليل غرض الآية، فإنها خرجت مخرج التمدح وبدخول أفعال العباد تحتها يزول معنى التمدح بل يثبت معنى يوجب الذم، وهذا لأن من جملة أفعال العباد ما هو افتراء على الله تعالى ووصف له بما لا يليق بصفاته وشتم له وقتل أوليائه، وبسط اليد واللسان في رسله وأنبيائه، ومقابله سفرائه إلى خلقه وأمنائه على وحيه ومبلغي أمره ونهيه بكل ما قدروا عليه من المكروه ووسعه طوقهم من الجفوة، والمتعرض لشتم نفسه والافتراء عليه سفه في الشاهد الذي هو دليل يبتنى عليه أمور الغائب، فكيف الموجد لذلك والمخرج له من
And the proof for the People of Truth is His statement, the Exalted: 'Creator of everything' (Surah al-Ra'd 13:16). And the acts of servants are things, so Allah Most High is their Creator by the generality of the verse. And the opponents object to that, saying: The acts of servants are excluded from this verse by evidence of the purpose of the verse, for it was issued in the manner of praise, and if the acts of servants enter under it, the meaning of praise ceases; rather, a meaning that necessitates blame is established. This is because among the acts of servants are slander against Allah Most High, describing Him with what is not befitting His attributes, abuse of Him, killing of His saints, stretching of hand and tongue against His messengers and prophets, and treating His ambassadors to His creation, His trustees over His revelation, and conveyers of His command and prohibition with all the harm they were capable of and the rudeness their capacity allowed. And he who subjects himself to abuse and slander is foolish in the witnessed realm, which is the evidence upon which matters of the unseen are based. So how could the one who brings that into existence and brings it forth be...
Source pages p. 858

Commentary
This passage begins with the proof of the People of Truth (Ahl al-Haqq) for the doctrine that God is the creator of all things, including human acts. The proof is based on the Quranic verse 'خَلِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ' (Creator of everything) in Surah al-Ra'd. Since human acts are things, they are included in the generality of the verse, making God their creator. The author then presents the objection from the Mu'tazila (the opponents). They argue that the verse is meant to be praise of God, but if human acts—which include evil deeds like slander against God, killing prophets, etc.—are also created by God, then the verse would not be praise but blame. Therefore, they conclude that human acts must be excluded from the generality of the verse. The objection is based on the 'purpose' (gharad) of the verse: it was revealed to extol God, and including evil human acts would contradict that purpose. The Mu'tazila support this by pointing to the evident foolishness of someone who slanders himself in the witnessed world, and then analogize that to the unseen: if a person does evil, attributing that evil to God would imply foolishness in God, which is impossible. The passage ends abruptly with the phrase 'فكيف الموجد لذلك والمخرج له من' (So how could the one who brings that into existence and brings it forth be...), which is incomplete; the response of the author, refuting the objection, would follow in the subsequent pages. This passage is a clear example of a kalam argument using scriptural proof and rational objection.

عموم الآية
غرض الآية
تمددح
افتراء
شاهد
غائب

Checkpoint
On what basis do the Mu'tazila argue that human acts are excluded from the general verse 'خَلِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ'?
A) Because human acts are not things.
B) Because the purpose of the verse is praise, and including evil human acts would turn it into blame.
C) Because the verse is abrogated.
D) Because human acts are not created by God.

Key Takeaway
The verse 'Creator of everything' provides a strong proof for God's creation of all things, but the Mu'tazila object that including evil acts contradicts the verse's purpose of praise, creating a key point of debate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Mu'tazili objection that including human acts would turn the verse from praise to blame, does it resonate with any hidden belief you hold about God's involvement in your own sinful choices? How do you personally resolve this without dismissing the verse's generality?
?
The verse 'Creator of everything' includes your every action—good and bad. Can you truly accept that God creates even your moments of disobedience? What does that mean for your understanding of your own moral responsibility and God's ultimate wisdom?
?
The Mu'tazila use an analogy from the witnessed world (a foolish person slandering himself) to argue against God creating evil. Do you find that analogy compelling or flawed? What does your answer reveal about your view of God's transcendence?

The Grammatical Rule of 'ما' in 'وما تعملون'
Nasafi presents the grammatical rule that 'ما' with verb indicates the masdar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the grammatical argument that the word 'ما' in 'وما تعملون' refers to the action (masdar) rather than the object, and how this supports the doctrine that human actions are created by Allah.

Core Idea
A single Arabic word 'ما' determines a major theological doctrine.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi delves into Arabic grammar to counter the Mu'tazilah interpretation of a key Quranic verse. He shows that the word 'ما' when attached to a verb indicates the action itself, not the object. This grammatical insight is crucial for understanding that Allah creates both humans and their actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the overall flow.
2
Identify the rule
Notice how Nasafi claims that 'ما' with a verb indicates the masdar. Find the example he gives.
3
Analyze the objection and answer
Read the Mu'tazilah objection and Nasafi's answer citing Sibawayh and the pronoun distinction.
Pay attention to the difference when the pronoun is present.
4
Understand the challenge
Nasafi ends by challenging opponents to produce evidence. Reflect on why this is important.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أي وعملكم فإن كلمة ما إذا اتصلت بالفعل صارا عبارة عن المصدر تقول: أعجبني ما صنعت أي صنعك، والخصوم يعترضون على هذا ويقولون: المراد منه المعمول أي خلقكم ومعمولكم وهي الأصنام المعمولة وهي أجسام ولا خلاف في كونها مخلوقة نظيره قوله تعالى: أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ وهم ما كانوا يعبدون فعلهم الذي هو النحت بل كانوا يعبدون المنحوت، وكذا قوله: تَلْقَفُ مَا يَأْفِكُونَ. والجواب أن كلمة ما إذا اتصلت بالفعل كان مجموعها عبارة عن المصدر عند الإطلاق هذا هو مذهب سيبويه وإن خالفه الأخفش في ذلك حيث جوز سيبويه أن يقال أعجبني ما قمت أي قيامك، ولو كان ذا عبارة عن المفعول لما جاز ذلك إلا في الفعل المتعدي، والأخفش لا يجوزه إلا في المعتدي، غير أن العارفين بكلام العرب المتبحرين في علم النحو مالوا إلى تصحيح قول سيبويه، وإذا ذكر العائد وهو الهاء فقيل: أعجبني ما صنعته حينئذ تكون عبارة عن المفعول، وفي كل موضع جعل عبارة عن المفعول كان بإضمار الهاء وهو عدول عن ظاهر الكلام بالدليل ولا دليل فمن ادعى قيام الدليل فليبرزوه، والدليل على أنه عند الإطلاق ينصرف إلى ما بينا قوله تعالى: جَزَاء بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ أي بعملهم دون معمولهم، وقال تعالى: ادْخُلُوا الْجَنَّةَ بِمَا كُنتُمْ تَعْمَلُونَ أي بعملكم إذ الجزاء يكون بالعمل دون المعمول، وكذا دخول الجنة، وكذا في قوله تعالى: أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ أي نحتكم لأنهم لما كانوا لا يعبدون تلك الأعيان إلا بعدما نحتوا ولم يروها مستحقة للعبادة إلا به صاروا في الحقيقة عابدين نحتهم دون منحوتهم. ومما يتعجب منه العاقل أن المعتزلة يتعلقون في المسألة بقوله تعالى: مَا جَعَلَ اللَّهُ من بحيرة والآية، ويصرفون ذلك إلى فعلهم في هذه الأعيان، ولا شك أن المذكور في الآية أعيان لا أفعال، ثم إذا آل الأمر إلى هذا الذي هو اسم الفعل صرفوه إلى محل الفعل وبمثل هذا يتبين أنهم يلعبون بكتاب الله ويحملونه على ما تميل إليه أهواؤهم دون ما توجبه حقائق الأدلة، على أنا وإن صرفنا الآية إلى المعمول، وجعلنا كأنه قال: والله خلقكم ومعمولكم فالاستدلال بالآية باق لأن الله تعالى لم يكن خالقا للمعمول لو لم يكن عملهم مخلوقا له لأن ذلك الجسم بدون عمل العباد لا وهو تعالى أثبت الخلق للمعمول فدل أن العمل الذي صار به الجسم يكون معمولاً.
That is, your action. For the word 'ma' when attached to a verb, both together become an expression of the infinitive (al-masdar). You say: 'I liked what you made' meaning your making. And the opponents object to this and say: the intended meaning is the object made (al-ma'mool), i.e., He created you and your made thing, and they are the idols which are made, and they are bodies, and there is no disagreement that they are created. A similar case is His statement: 'Do you worship what you carve?' and they did not worship their action which is carving, but they worshipped the carved thing. And likewise His statement: 'It swallows what they faked.' And the answer is that the word 'ma' when attached to the verb, the total of them is an expression of the infinitive in unrestricted use; this is the madhhab of Sibawayh, although al-Akhfash differed with him in that. For Sibawayh allowed that one says 'I liked what you stood' meaning your standing, and if it were an expression of the object, that would not be permissible except with a transitive verb, and al-Akhfash only allows it with transitive verbs. However, those knowledgeable of the speech of the Arabs, well-versed in the science of grammar, inclined to correct the saying of Sibawayh. And when the referent (al-aa'id), which is the pronoun (al-haa), is mentioned, and it is said 'I liked what I made it' then it becomes an expression of the object. And in every place where it is made an expression of the object, it is by the suppression of the pronoun, and that is a deviation from the apparent meaning of speech by evidence, and there is no evidence. So whoever claims the existence of evidence, let them produce it. The evidence that it refers in unrestricted use to what we have stated is His statement: 'Recompense for what they used to do' i.e., for their action, not their made thing. And He said: 'Enter Paradise for what you used to do' i.e., for your action, because recompense is for the action, not the made thing. And likewise entering Paradise. And likewise in His statement: 'Do you worship what you carve?' i.e., your carving, because since they did not worship those entities except after they carved them and did not consider them worthy of worship except thereby, they became in reality worshippers of their carving, not their carved thing. And among things that the rational person wonders about is that the Mu'tazilah cling in this issue to His statement: 'Allah has not made any Bahirah' and the verse, and they turn that to their action concerning these entities. There is no doubt that what is mentioned in the verse are entities, not actions. Then when the matter comes to this, which is the verbal noun (ism al-fi'l), they turn it to the locus of the action. By such it becomes clear that they play with the Book of Allah and interpret it according to what their desires incline, not what the realities of evidence necessitate. Moreover, even if we turn the verse to the object made, and we make it as if He said: 'And Allah created you and your made thing,' the inference from the verse remains, because Allah would not be the Creator of the made thing if their action were not created by Him, because that body without the action of the servants is not, and He—exalted—affirmed creation for the made thing, so it indicates that the action by which the body becomes (an object) is created.
Source pages p. 868

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical and theological argument defending the Ash'ari/Maturidi doctrine that human actions are created by Allah, against the Mu'tazilah interpretation of the verse 'والله خلقكم وما تعملون' (Q. 37:96). The author (Imam Nasafi) begins by stating that the phrase 'وما تعملون' refers to the action (the masdar), not the product (the ma'mool). He explains that when the word 'ما' is attached to a verb, the combination indicates the infinitive, as in the example 'أعجبني ما صنعت' meaning 'your making'. The opponents (likely Mu'tazilah) object that it means 'your made thing' i.e., the idols they carve. The author then refutes this by citing the authoritative grammatical rule of Sibawayh, which states that 'ما' with a verb indicates the masdar in unrestricted speech. He acknowledges that al-Akhfash disagreed, but notes that the majority of grammarians support Sibawayh. The author also provides evidence from other Quranic verses where 'ما' with a verb is interpreted as the action (e.g., 'جزاء بما كانوا يعملون' meaning 'recompense for their action', and 'ادخلوا الجنة بما كنتم تعملون' meaning 'for your action'). He further argues that in the verse about worshipping carved idols, the true object of worship is the carving act itself, since they only worship after carving. Next, the author criticizes the Mu'tazilah for inconsistently interpreting another verse about 'بحيرة' (Bahirah) as referring to actions rather than entities, while here they insist on entities. He accuses them of playing with Allah's Book. Finally, he makes a decisive point: even if one interprets 'وما تعملون' as 'your made thing' (i.e., idols), the argument for creation of actions still holds, because the body (idol) does not exist without the servant's action of carving; thus Allah's creation of the made thing implies the creation of the action by which it becomes made. This refutes the Mu'tazilah position that human actions are uncreated.

Key Terms
ما المصدرية
المصدر
المفعول
سيبويه
الأخفش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'وما تعملون' refers to the objects made (idols) rather than the action.
Correction: Grammatically, 'ما' + verb indicates the action (masdar), not the object. The verse supports creation of actions.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what does the phrase 'أعجبني ما صنعت' primarily refer to?
A) I liked what you made (the object)
B) I liked your making (the action)
C) I liked what you did it
D) I liked something else

Key Takeaway
The grammatical interpretation of 'ما' is decisive for proving that Allah creates human actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Qur'an, do you rely on quick translations or do you pause to consider the precise grammatical structures that could change the entire meaning of a verse? How can you cultivate a habit of deeper linguistic reflection?
?
This passage shows that a single word ('ما') can determine whether we attribute actions to ourselves or to Allah. Are there areas in your life where you claim ownership of your deeds, forgetting that the very act of doing is created by Allah? How would acknowledging this change your attitude toward success and failure?
?
Sibawayh's rule is upheld by the majority, but the opponents demanded evidence for their interpretation. Are you willing to subject your own beliefs to the same scrutiny? What evidence do you have for the positions you hold about divine decree, and are you prepared to defend them with rigorous reasoning?

Quranic Evidence and Final Proof for Creation of Actions
Nasafi provides Quranic evidence and a final logical proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses Quranic verses and logical reasoning to refute the Mu'tazilah claim that human actions are not created by Allah.

Core Idea
Quranic consistency proves that actions, not objects, are recompensed.

After establishing the grammatical rule, Nasafi turns to additional Quranic evidence to solidify his position. He shows that recompense is for actions, not for objects, and that even the Mu'tazilah's own argument from the Bahirah verse backfires. Finally, he provides a logical proof that if Allah creates the made thing, He must also create the action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the flow of evidence.
2
Examine the Quranic proofs
Note the three Quranic verses Nasafi uses and how each supports the action meaning.
3
Grasp the critique
Understand the Mu'tazilah inconsistency with the Bahirah verse and Nasafi's accusation.
4
Follow the final argument
Trace the logical argument: even if the verse means object, the action must be created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أي وعملكم فإن كلمة ما إذا اتصلت بالفعل صارا عبارة عن المصدر تقول: أعجبني ما صنعت أي صنعك، والخصوم يعترضون على هذا ويقولون: المراد منه المعمول أي خلقكم ومعمولكم وهي الأصنام المعمولة وهي أجسام ولا خلاف في كونها مخلوقة نظيره قوله تعالى: أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ وهم ما كانوا يعبدون فعلهم الذي هو النحت بل كانوا يعبدون المنحوت، وكذا قوله: تَلْقَفُ مَا يَأْفِكُونَ. والجواب أن كلمة ما إذا اتصلت بالفعل كان مجموعها عبارة عن المصدر عند الإطلاق هذا هو مذهب سيبويه وإن خالفه الأخفش في ذلك حيث جوز سيبويه أن يقال أعجبني ما قمت أي قيامك، ولو كان ذا عبارة عن المفعول لما جاز ذلك إلا في الفعل المتعدي، والأخفش لا يجوزه إلا في المعتدي، غير أن العارفين بكلام العرب المتبحرين في علم النحو مالوا إلى تصحيح قول سيبويه، وإذا ذكر العائد وهو الهاء فقيل: أعجبني ما صنعته حينئذ تكون عبارة عن المفعول، وفي كل موضع جعل عبارة عن المفعول كان بإضمار الهاء وهو عدول عن ظاهر الكلام بالدليل ولا دليل فمن ادعى قيام الدليل فليبرزوه، والدليل على أنه عند الإطلاق ينصرف إلى ما بينا قوله تعالى: جَزَاء بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ أي بعملهم دون معمولهم، وقال تعالى: ادْخُلُوا الْجَنَّةَ بِمَا كُنتُمْ تَعْمَلُونَ أي بعملكم إذ الجزاء يكون بالعمل دون المعمول، وكذا دخول الجنة، وكذا في قوله تعالى: أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ أي نحتكم لأنهم لما كانوا لا يعبدون تلك الأعيان إلا بعدما نحتوا ولم يروها مستحقة للعبادة إلا به صاروا في الحقيقة عابدين نحتهم دون منحوتهم. ومما يتعجب منه العاقل أن المعتزلة يتعلقون في المسألة بقوله تعالى: مَا جَعَلَ اللَّهُ من بحيرة والآية، ويصرفون ذلك إلى فعلهم في هذه الأعيان، ولا شك أن المذكور في الآية أعيان لا أفعال، ثم إذا آل الأمر إلى هذا الذي هو اسم الفعل صرفوه إلى محل الفعل وبمثل هذا يتبين أنهم يلعبون بكتاب الله ويحملونه على ما تميل إليه أهواؤهم دون ما توجبه حقائق الأدلة، على أنا وإن صرفنا الآية إلى المعمول، وجعلنا كأنه قال: والله خلقكم ومعمولكم فالاستدلال بالآية باق لأن الله تعالى لم يكن خالقا للمعمول لو لم يكن عملهم مخلوقا له لأن ذلك الجسم بدون عمل العباد لا وهو تعالى أثبت الخلق للمعمول فدل أن العمل الذي صار به الجسم يكون معمولاً.

The author then refutes this by citing the authoritative grammatical rule of Sibawayh, which states that 'ما' with a verb indicates the masdar in unrestricted speech. He acknowledges that al-Akhfash disagreed, but notes that the majority of grammarians support Sibawayh. The author also provides evidence from other Quranic verses where 'ما' with a verb is interpreted as the action (e.g., 'جزاء بما كانوا يعملون' meaning 'recompense for their action', and 'ادخلوا الجنة بما كنتم تعملون' meaning 'for your action'). He further argues that in the verse about worshipping carved idols, the true object of worship is the carving act itself, since they only worship after carving. Next, the author criticizes the Mu'tazilah for inconsistently interpreting another verse about 'بحيرة' (Bahirah) as referring to actions rather than entities, while here they insist on entities. He accuses them of playing with Allah's Book. Finally, he makes a decisive point: even if one interprets 'وما تعملون' as 'your made thing' (i.e., idols), the argument for creation of actions still holds, because the body (idol) does not exist without the servant's action of carving; thus Allah's creation of the made thing implies the creation of the action by which it becomes made. This refutes the Mu'tazilah position that human actions are uncreated.

Key Terms
جزاء
البحيرة
خلق الأفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilah believe that humans create their own actions independently of Allah.
Correction: Nasafi shows that even if the verse refers to objects, the action that produces the object is created by Allah.

Checkpoint
What does the verse 'جزاء بما كانوا يعملون' indicate according to Nasafi?
A) Recompense for the actions performed
B) Recompense for the idols worshipped
C) Recompense for both actions and objects
D) Recompense for something else

Key Takeaway
Even if 'ما تعملون' means the object, the action needed to make that object must also be created by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you truly believe that Allah created that action in you? How does that affect your humility in success and your hope for reward? Take a moment to thank Allah for creating that action in you right now.
?
The Mu'tazilah were accused of twisting the Quran to fit their desires. Examine your own heart: are there any verses of the Quran you have interpreted in a way that makes you comfortable with your sins or neglect? Commit to seeking the sound understanding from the scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah.
?
If every action you do is created by Allah, then you have no independent power. Does that make you feel helpless or responsible? How can you reconcile this with the commands of Allah to do good and avoid evil? Spend a minute in prostration asking Allah to make your actions pleasing to Him.

Refuting the Mu'tazila Interpretation of 'Wa Ma Ta'malun'
Al-Nasafi refutes Mu'tazila interpretation of 'Wa Ma Ta'malun'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Nasafi's refutation of the Mu'tazila claim that the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' refers only to objects, not actions, and how he uses their own principle against them.

Core Idea
Even if the verse meant objects, God creates the action that makes them objects.

In this passage, Al-Nasafi takes on the Mu'tazila interpretation of a key Qur'anic verse used in the debate on human action. He shows how their reading is inconsistent and how even conceding their interpretation does not save their argument. Then he delivers a powerful refutation based on their own principle of identity between act and object.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main argument
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice that Al-Nasafi begins with astonishment at the Mu'tazila's method.
Pay attention to the shift from astonishment to logical refutation.
2
Analyze the first refutation: Even if 'what you do' means the object, the action must be created
Al-Nasafi argues that God creating the object implies He creates the action that makes it an object.
This is a conditional argument.
3
Examine the weak answer and its criticism
Some theologians tried to say the word means both, but Al-Nasafi dismisses that as unsound.
Why is it unsound? Because it forces the common term to include both, which is not proper.
4
Understand the refutation based on the Mu'tazila's own principle
They believe act and object are identical. Al-Nasafi shows that if so, the verse cannot refer to the idol (not a work), but to the act (carving) which is identical to the object.
This is a brilliant internal critique.
5
Summarize the overall refutation
Write a short summary of how Al-Nasafi defends the doctrine that God creates human actions.
Make sure to include the key terms: fi'l, maf'ul, 'amal, ma'mul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يتعجب منه العاقل أن المعتزلة يتعلقون في المسألة بقوله تعالى: ﴿ مَا جَعَلَ اللَّهُ من بحيرة ﴾ والآية، ويصرفون ذلك إلى فعلهم في هذه الأعيان، ولا شك أن المذكور في الآية أعيان لا أفعال، ثم إذا آل الأمر إلى هذا الذي هو اسم الفعل صرفوه إلى محل الفعل وبمثل هذا يتبين أنهم يلعبون بكتاب الله ويحملونه على ما تميل إليه أهواؤهم دون ما توجبه حقائق الأدلة، على أنا وإن صرفنا الآية إلى المعمول، وجعلنا كأنه قال: والله خلقكم ومعمولكم فالاستدلال بالآية باق لأن الله تعالى لم يكن خالقا للمعمول لو لم يكن عملهم مخلوقا له لأن ذلك الجسم بدون عمل العباد لا وهو تعالى أثبت الخلق للمعمول فدل أن العمل الذي صار به الجسم يكون معمولاً. وبعض المتكلمين أجاب أن الآية لما احتملت الأمرين أعني أن هذه اللفظة لما كانت تذكر ويراد بها المعمول، وتذكر ويراد بها العمل حملت عليهما جميعًا، ولكن فيه وهاء لما فيه من جعل المشترك مشتملاً وهو غير سديد. ثم مما يبطل التأويل على أصل المعتزلة أن عندهم الفعل والمفعول واحد فكان العمل والمعمول واحدًا، والصنم ليس بعمل للعبد فلا يكون معموله، فأما الفعل في الصنم فهو فعل العبد فكان هو بعينه معموله فانصرفت إليه الآية بخلاف قوله تعالى: ﴿ أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ ﴾ لأن النحت غير المنحوت، ولا اتحاد بينهما عندهم، وكان المنحوت عين الصنم، وأما فيما نحن فيه فبخلافه، والله الموفق. وبهذا يجيبهم من زعم اتحاد الفعل والمفعول ممن ساعدنا في هذه المسألة وبالله المعونة.
Among things that amaze the rational person is that the Mu'tazila cling in this matter to His statement: 'Allah has not made (the animal) Bahirah' and the verse, and they turn that to their action in these entities, and there is no doubt that what is mentioned in the verse are entities, not actions. Then when the matter comes to this which is the verbal noun (ism al-fi'l), they turn it to the locus of the action. By such it becomes clear that they play with the Book of Allah and interpret it according to what their whims incline to, not according to what the realities of evidences require. Nevertheless, even if we interpret the verse as referring to the object (al-ma'mul), and we make it as if He said: 'Allah created you and your object,' the inference from the verse remains, because Allah would not be the creator of the object if their action were not created by Him, for that body without the action of the servants is not, and He has established creation for the object, so it indicates that the action by which the body becomes an object is created. Some theologians answered that since the verse admits both meanings—i.e., this word is sometimes mentioned meaning the object and sometimes mentioned meaning the action—it is applied to both. But there is weakness in this because it makes the common term include both, which is not sound. Then, among things that invalidate the interpretation according to the Mu'tazila's own principle is that with them the act (al-fi'l) and the object (al-maf'ul) are identical, so the work (al-'amal) and the object (al-ma'mul) would be identical. The idol is not a work of the servant, so it would not be his object. As for the act in the idol, it is the act of the servant, so it itself is his object; thus the verse refers to it, unlike His statement: 'Do you worship what you carve?' because carving is other than the carved, and there is no identity between them according to them, and the carved is the very idol. But in our case it is otherwise. And Allah is the grantor of success. And with this he answers those who claim the identity of act and object among those who agree with us in this matter. And with Allah is assistance.
Source pages p. 869

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila's interpretation of the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' (Surah as-Saffat 37:96). Al-Nasafi first expresses astonishment that the Mu'tazila cling to a verse about entities (the Bahirah) but turn it to their actions, showing they play with God's book. He then argues that even if we interpret 'what you do' as the object (ma'mul) rather than the action, the verse still proves that God creates the action, because the object would not exist without the action. Without the servant's action, the body would not be an object; since God created the object, He must have created the action that makes it an object. Next, he criticizes a weak answer by some theologians who say the word can mean both action and object, calling it unsound. Then he refutes the Mu'tazila on their own principle: they hold that act (fi'l) and object (maf'ul) are identical. If so, then work ('amal) and object (ma'mul) are identical. But the idol is not a work of the servant (it is not their action), so it cannot be their object. However, the act performed on the idol (carving) is the servant's act and is identical with their object. So the verse about 'what you do' refers to the act, not the idol, unlike the verse about carving. This refutes the Mu'tazila who deny that human actions are created by God.

Key Terms
فعل
مفعول
عمل
معمول
اتحاد الفعل والمفعول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Allah created you and what you do' can only refer to objects (like idols), so it does not prove God creates actions.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that even if the verse refers to objects, God must create the action that makes those objects, and the Mu'tazila's own principle of identity between act and object actually supports that the verse refers to the act.

Checkpoint

B) Even if the verse refers to objects, God must have created the action that makes those objects.
C) The Mu'tazila principle of identity between act and object supports their view.
D) The word 'ma'mul' is ambiguous and should be ignored.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazila by showing that even if the verse refers to objects, God creates the action, and their own identity principle turns against them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your daily actions—praying, eating, speaking—do you truly acknowledge that each action is created by Allah and not by your own independent power? What would change in your humility before Him if you internalized this?
?
Al-Nasafi warns against 'playing with the Book of Allah' to suit one's whims. Have you ever interpreted a verse of the Quran in a way that justified a desire or habit you were reluctant to give up? How can you guard against this in your own heart?
?
If your every action is created by Allah, then what is your role? Does this make you more grateful for the ability to act, or more fearful of misusing the actions He creates through you? Commit to one concrete way to increase your reliance on Allah in your actions tomorrow.

Three Rational Topics on Human Actions for Ahl al-Sunna
Imam Nasafi enumerates three rational topics on human actions for Ahl al-Sunna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational topics that form the foundation of the Ahl al-Sunna position on human actions.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Sunna's rational stance on human actions rests on three key topics.

Imam Nasafi presents three rational topics that define the Ahl al-Sunna position on human actions. These topics address the nature of divine power, human agency, and the coexistence of two powers on a single act. Understanding these three points is essential for grasping the Maturidi approach to qadar.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Begin by reading the Arabic text and the literal English translation. Note the three distinct topics the author enumerates.
2
Identify the first topic
Focus on the first topic: the impossibility of anyone other than God possessing the power of creation. Why is this a crucial starting point?
This establishes tawhid in creation.
3
Identify the second topic
The second topic affirms that the servant has an action without having creative power, and is not compelled. This distinguishes Ahl al-Sunna from both Jabrites and Mu'tazilites.
4
Identify the third topic
The third topic states that one object of power can fall under two powers—this is possible, not impossible. This directly rebuts the Mu'tazilite objection.
Key point for the concept of kasb.
5
Reflect on the overall structure
Consider how these three topics together form a coherent rational defense of the Ahl al-Sunna position. Why are all three necessary?
Each addresses a different front of the debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأدلة العقلية لأهل السنة في أفعال العباد: وأما المعقول لنا في المسألة فنقول – وبالله التوفيق: إن الكلام في المسألة يقع في مواضع أحدها في إثبات الاستحالة لثبوت قدرة التخليق لغير الله تعالى. والثاني: في أن العبد له فعل وإن لم يكن له قدرة التخليق، وليس بمضطر فيه. والثالث: في أن دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين من جملة المجوزات دون الممتنعات.
The rational proofs of Ahl al-Sunna on the actions of servants: As for what is rational for us in the issue, we say – and with God is success: Verily the discourse on the issue falls into topics: one of them is the establishment of the impossibility of the existence of the power of creation (qudrat al-takhlīq) for anyone other than God, exalted. The second is that the servant has an action (fi'l) even if he does not have the power of creation, and he is not compelled (muḍṭarr) in it. The third is that the entry of one object of power (maqdūr) under the power of two powerful beings (qādirān) is among the possibilities (al-mujawwazāt), not among the impossibilities (al-mumtani'āt).
Source pages p. 871

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the rational proofs (الأدلة العقلية) that Ahl al-Sunna use regarding the issue of human actions (أفعال العباد). Imam Nasafi states that the discussion on this issue falls into three topics (مواضع). The first topic is proving the impossibility (الاستحالة) of the power of creation (قدرة التخليق) belonging to anyone other than God. This means that no creature can bring something into existence from nothing; only God can create. The second topic is that the servant does have an action (فعل) – i.e., he is an agent – even though he does not possess the power of creation. This affirms human agency without ascribing creative power to the human. Moreover, the servant is not compelled (مضطر) in his action; he acts by his own choice, though his power is created by God. The third topic is that it is possible (جائز) for one single object of power (مقدور واحد) to fall under the power of two powerful beings (قادرين). This is a key point in the debate with the Mu'tazilites, who held that one act cannot be the result of two agents. Ahl al-Sunna affirm that it is within God's power to make one act dependent on both God's creation and the servant's acquisition (كسب). The author categorizes this as among the possibilities (المجوزات) and not impossibilities (الممتنعات). These three topics together form the rational foundation of the Ash'ari/Maturidi position on human action.

Key Terms
دليل عقلي
فعل
قدرة التخليق
عبد
مضطر
مقدور
قادران
جائز
ممتنع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human actions are either entirely from God (so humans are compelled) or entirely from humans (so humans are independent creators).
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna hold that human actions are real but not created by humans; God creates the action while the servant acquires it. The third topic shows that one act can be under two powers, allowing for both divine creation and human acquisition.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Nasafi, what is the third topic in the rational discussion of human actions?
A) The servant is compelled in his actions.
B) The impossibility of anyone other than God having the power of creation.
C) The possibility of one object of power falling under the power of two powerful beings.
D) The servant has no action at all.

Key Takeaway
The Ahl al-Sunna rational position on human actions rests on three principles: only God creates, humans act without creating, and one act can be under two powers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you truly own that action, or do you feel it was inevitable because God decreed it? Based on this lesson, what is your real accountability before Allah today?
?
If you truly believe that only God possesses the power to create, how does that reshape your reliance on Him in your daily actions—especially those you think you control? Will you consciously attribute your next success or failure to Him alone?
?
The lesson teaches that your action is yours without you being a creator. Does your self-worth depend more on your achievements (as if you created them) or on your obedience to the One who creates outcomes? What in your life needs to change to align with this?

The Knowledge Requirement for Creative Power
Nasafi argues that human ignorance of the details of action proves they lack creative power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that human ignorance of the details of action proves they lack the power to create their own actions.

Core Idea
Creative power requires detailed knowledge, and humans are ignorant of how actions come to be.

This lesson presents a key argument from Imam Nasafi on the question of human agency. His opponents, the Mu'tazila, conceded that a perfectly crafted action must come from a knowledgeable agent. Nasafi uses their own concession to show that since humans are ignorant of the inner workings of their actions, they cannot be the creators of those actions. The argument is simple yet profound.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the full English translation. This will give you the complete argument in the author's own words.
Notice that the passage is cut off, but the core argument is complete.
2
Identify the key premise
The author begins by noting that even the opponents agree that a perfect, precise action requires a knowledgeable agent. This is the foundation of the argument.
This premise is intuitive: we naturally judge that a well-made product comes from a skilled maker.
3
Apply the premise to human actions
Nasafi then applies this premise: if humans had creative power over their actions, they would need to know all the details of how the action comes into existence. Since we observe humans are ignorant of these details, they cannot be creators.
The author gives examples: we cannot conceive how something emerges from nothing, nor do we know the exact space and parts involved in a simple movement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما مساعدة الخصوم فإنهم ساعدونا أن من شرط خروج الفعل محكمًا متقنا كون الفاعل عالما بذلك، ولذا كان الفعل المحكم المتقن دليل كون الفاعل عالمًا وإن لم يكن عند الكعبي دليلا على العلم لا في الشاهد ولا في الغائب، وعند الجبائي يكون دليلاً على العلم لا في الشاهد دون الغائب على ما سبق في مسألة الصفات وكذا شهادات المعارف، فإن كون الفعل المحكم المتقن مفتقرا إلى كون الفاعل له عالما به مما تمكّن في بداهة العقول وأوائل الفكر، حتى إن من رأى فعلاً محكمًا متقنا حكم بأول الفكرة وسابق البديهة بكون فاعله عالما حاذقا في الصناعة، ومن جوز حصول مثله ممن لا علم له به تسارع الناس إلى تسفيهه ونسبته إلى الغباوة والجهل، وإذا ثبتت هذه القاعدة فنقول : لو كان للعبد قدرة تخليق فعله لكان ينبغي أن يكون له العلم بكيفية خروجه من العدم إلى الوجود وبما يخرج عليه فعله من المقادير والأحوال والأوصاف، وحيث رأينا جهله بهذه المعاني وانعدام علمه بها دل أن لا قدرة له على فعله من حيث التخليق. ألا ترى أنه لو كان جاهلا بالفعل أصلا لكان خارجا عن قدرته أصلا، فإذا كان جاهلا بالتخليق كان ذلك خارجا عن قدرته، ولا شك في جهله بما بينا فإنه لاشك أنه لا يقدر في عقله كيفية خروج الشيء من العدم إلى الوجود، ولا يتصور ذلك أيضا في وهمه فما ينبغي أن يكون له عليه من حيث التخليق قدرة، وكذا لا يبلغ علمه مقدار فعله ويقصر عن الوقوف على القدر الذي يشغله من الهواء والمكان وعدد أجزاء المكان الذي قطعه بتحريك يده وبقطع كل جزء لا يتجزأ من
And as for the concession of the opponents, they conceded to us that among the conditions for an action to emerge perfect and precise is that the agent be knowledgeable of it. Hence the perfect, precise action is evidence of the agent's being knowledgeable, even if according to al-Ka'bi it is not evidence for knowledge either in the witnessed or the unseen, and according to al-Jubba'i it is evidence for knowledge in the witnessed but not in the unseen, as preceded in the issue of attributes, and likewise the testimonies of the intellects. For the fact that the perfect, precise action depends on its agent being knowledgeable of it is firmly established in the primordial nature of intellects and the first thoughts, such that whoever sees a perfect, precise action judges at first thought and immediate intuition that its agent is knowledgeable and skilled in the craft. And whoever allows the occurrence of such a thing from one who has no knowledge of it, people hasten to declare him foolish and attribute him to stupidity and ignorance. And when this principle is established, we say: If the servant had the power to create his action, he would have to have knowledge of how it emerges from non-existence to existence, and of the quantities, states, and attributes upon which his action emerges. And since we see his ignorance of these meanings and the absence of his knowledge of them, it indicates that he has no power over his action in terms of creation. Do you not see that if he were ignorant of the action entirely, it would be completely outside his power? So if he is ignorant of its creation, that is outside his power. There is no doubt about his ignorance of what we have explained, for there is no doubt that he cannot conceive in his mind the manner of a thing's emergence from non-existence to existence, nor can he imagine it in his estimation. So it should not be that he has power over it in terms of creation. Likewise, his knowledge does not reach the measure of his action and falls short of grasping the amount it occupies of air and space and the number of parts of the space that he traverses by moving his hand and by cutting each indivisible part of...
Source pages p. 875

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof that humans cannot create (takhliq) their own actions. It begins by noting that even the opponents (the Mu'tazila) concede that a perfect, precise action requires an agent who knows it. This is an intuitive principle: when we see a well-made product, we immediately judge that its maker is knowledgeable. The author then applies this principle: if humans had the power to create their actions, they would need to know the detailed process of bringing them from non-existence to existence, including quantities, states, and attributes. However, we observe that humans are ignorant of these details; they cannot comprehend how an action comes into being or even imagine it. Therefore, they cannot have creative power over their actions. The author reinforces this with an analogy: being ignorant of an action entirely means it is outside one's power, so ignorance of its creation must also exclude it from one's power. He concludes that human knowledge falls short of even grasping the space and parts involved in a simple movement, so they cannot be creators.

Key Terms
مساعدة الخصوم
قدرة تخليق
بداهة العقول
فعل محكم متقن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human power over actions is like divine creative power.
Correction: The author distinguishes by showing that creative power requires detailed knowledge, which humans lack.

Checkpoint
What is the key premise that the author uses to prove that humans cannot create their own actions?
A) Humans are ignorant of the future.
B) A perfect action requires a knowing agent.
C) The Mu'tazila deny human power.
D) Actions are not real entities.

Key Takeaway
Human ignorance of the how of creation proves that whatever power we have over our actions is not a creative power like Allah's.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform even the smallest action, like moving your hand, you are unable to explain how it comes into existence from nothing. How does this ignorance humble you and remind you of your absolute dependence on Allah's creation?
?
In what areas of your life are you tempted to claim control or independence, forgetting that you lack the knowledge to create even a single moment of your existence? How does this lesson challenge that temptation?
?
If you truly believe that Allah creates every detail of your actions, including your most private thoughts and decisions, how should that change the way you approach your daily choices and their outcomes? Are you willing to surrender your illusion of self-sufficiency?

intermediate

Proof That Humans Cannot Create Their Actions
Nasafi proves humans cannot create actions due to ignorance of details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's proof that humans lack creative power over their actions because they are ignorant of the minute details of their own actions.

Core Idea
Creative power requires exhaustive knowledge; humans lack that knowledge.

Nasafi presents a powerful argument against those who claim humans create their own actions. He starts from a premise everyone accepts: a perfect action requires a knowledgeable agent. Then he shows that humans are completely ignorant of the intricate details of their actions—spatial, temporal, and moral—so they cannot have creative power. This lesson walks through his logical steps.

Guided Path
1
Understand the agreed premise
The opponents concede that a well-made, perfect action requires an agent who knows it. This is the foundation of the argument.
Even al-Ka'bi and al-Jubba'i differ on evidentiary scope but agree on the basic principle.
2
Apply the premise to human actions
If a human had the power to create his action, he would need to know every detail of its emergence and properties. Observe that humans are ignorant of these details.
Nasafi points to the inability to conceive how something comes from non-existence into existence.
3
Examine the three areas of ignorance
Nasafi highlights spatial parts (air, space), temporal parts (moments), and moral quality (good/evil). In each case, humans lack exhaustive knowledge.
For example, one cannot know the number of air particles displaced by a hand movement.
4
Consider the opponent's dilemma
The opponent must either concede the argument, falsely claim knowledge of these details, or admit ignorance yet still affirm creation—which contradicts the Quranic condition of knowledge for power.
This shows the strength of the proof.

وأما مساعدة الخصوم فإنهم ساعدونا أن من شرط خروج الفعل محكمًا متقنا كون الفاعل عالما بذلك، ولذا كان الفعل المحكم المتقن دليل كون الفاعل عالمًا وإن لم يكن عند الكعبي دليلا على العلم لا في الشاهد ولا في والجهل، وإذا ثبتت هذه القاعدة فنقول : لو كان للعبد قدرة تخليق فعله لكان ينبغي أن يكون له العلم بكيفية خروجه من العدم إلى الوجود وبما يخرج عليه فعله من المقادير والأحوال والأوصاف، وحيث رأينا جهله بهذه المعاني وانعدام علمه بها دل أن لا قدرة له على فعله من حيث التخليق. ألا ترى أنه لو كان جاهلا بالفعل أصلا لكان خارجا عن قدرته أصلا، فإذا كان جاهلا بالتخليق كان ذلك خارجا عن قدرته، ولا شك في جهله بما بينا فإنه لا شك أنه لا يقدر في عقله كيفية خروج الشيء من العدم إلى الوجود، ولا يتصور ذلك أيضا في وهمه فما ينبغي أن يكون له عليه من حيث التخليق قدرة، وكذا لا يبلغ علمه مقدار فعله ويقصر عن الوقوف على القدر الذي يشغله من الهواء والمكان وعدد أجزاء المكان الذي قطعه بتحريك يده وبقطع كل جزء لا يتجزأ من الهواء تحصل في يده حركة وبمجموع تلك الحركات يحصل ما قصد إليه من الفعل فإذا لم يكن عالما بعدد أجزاء الهواء والمكان لم يكن عالما بعدد الحركات التي حصل فيها الفعل الذي قصد فلم يكن عالما بقدر الفعل وكذا يكون جاهلا بقدر الزمان الذي يشغله بفعله وفي كل جزء لا يتجزأ من الزمان يحصل فعل على حدة، فكان الجهل بأجزاء الزمان جهلا بعدد الأفعال التي يحصل بمجموعها ما هو المقصود. وكذا يخرج عن حسن وقبح لا يبلغ علمه قدرهما بل يحصل اعتقاد الكافر والمبتدع على قبح لا علم لهما به البتة بل يظن كل واحد منهما أن اعتقاده في غاية الحسن ونهاية الصحة وهو موصوف بضد ذلك، ولما ثبت جهله بفعله من هذه الوجوه دل أن لا قدرة له عليه من هذه الوجوه، فكان من هذه الوجوه متعلقا بقدرة غيره وهو يعلم به من حيث إنه حركة أو سكونا طاعة أو معصية مأمور به أو منهي عنه، فكان له من هذه الوجوه عليه قدرة فإن ساعدت الخصوم على هذا فقد انقادوا للحق وأبطلوا مذهبهم، وإن ادعوا ثبوت علم للعبد بهذه الوجوه كابروا وعاندوا وادعوا ما يعرفون كذبهم فيه بيقين، وإن سلموا فقد العلم وثبوت الجهل بهذه الوجوه ومع ذلك أثبتوا للعباد قدرة الفعل مع جهلهم بهذه الوجوه فقد ناقضوا وعاندوا كتاب الله تعالى في جعله العلم بذلك شرطا لثبوت القدرة وخرجوا لنا
As for the concession to the opponents, they have conceded to us that from the condition of an action emerging well-made and perfect is that the agent be knowledgeable of it. Therefore, the well-made perfect action is evidence of the agent being knowledgeable, even if according to al-Ka'bi it is not evidence for knowledge neither in the witnessed nor in the unseen, and according to al-Jubba'i it is evidence for knowledge in the witnessed but not in the unseen, as preceded in the question of attributes and likewise the testimonies of cognitions. Indeed, the fact that a well-made perfect action is dependent on the agent being knowledgeable of it is firmly established in the innate disposition of intellects and the first thoughts. So much so that whoever sees a well-made perfect action judges at the first thought and the precedence of innate disposition that its agent is knowledgeable and skillful in the craft, and whoever permits the occurrence of the like of it from someone who has no knowledge of it, people hasten to declare him foolish and attribute him to stupidity and ignorance. When this principle is established, we say: If the servant had the power to create his action, then he should have knowledge of the manner of its emergence from non-existence into existence, and of the measures, states, and attributes upon which his action emerges. And since we see his ignorance of these meanings and the non-existence of his knowledge of them, this indicates that he has no power over his action in terms of creation. Do you not see that if he were ignorant of the action entirely, it would be entirely outside his power. So if he is ignorant of creation, then that is outside his power. And there is no doubt about his ignorance of what we have explained, for there is no doubt that he cannot in his intellect conceive the manner of a thing's emergence from non-existence into existence, nor can that be imagined in his estimation, so he should not have power over it in terms of creation. Likewise, his knowledge does not reach the measure of his action and falls short of grasping the amount that it occupies of air and space, and the number of parts of space he traverses by moving his hand. By each indivisible part of the air, a movement occurs in his hand, and by the sum of those movements what he intended of the action occurs. So if he is not knowledgeable of the number of parts of air and space, he is not knowledgeable of the number of movements in which the intended action occurs, so he is not knowledgeable of the measure of the action. Likewise, he is ignorant of the measure of time that his action occupies, and in each indivisible part of time a separate action occurs. So ignorance of the parts of time is ignorance of the number of actions by whose sum what is intended occurs. Likewise, regarding good and evil, his knowledge does not reach their measure. Rather, the belief of the disbeliever and the innovator arises about evil while they have no knowledge of it at all. Rather, each of them thinks that his belief is in the utmost good and extreme correctness, while he is described by the opposite of that. Since his ignorance of his action is established from these aspects, it indicates that he has no power over it from these aspects. So from these aspects, it is dependent on the power of another, while he knows it insofar as it is movement or stillness, obedience or disobedience, commanded or forbidden. So he has power over it from these aspects. If the opponents concede to this, then they have submitted to the truth and nullified their doctrine. And if they claim the establishment of knowledge for the servant regarding these aspects, they are obstinate and stubborn, claiming what they know to be false with certainty. And if they concede lack of knowledge and the establishment of ignorance regarding these aspects, yet still affirm for servants power over the action despite their ignorance of these aspects, then they have contradicted and opposed the Book of God Almighty in making knowledge a condition for the establishment of power, and they have departed from us.
Source pages p. 875

Commentary
This passage is a proof (dalil) that human beings do not have the power to create (takhliq) their own actions. The author, Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, builds his argument on a premise conceded by opponents: a well-made, perfect action requires an agent who has knowledge of it. He states this as a self-evident truth, even noting differences among theologians like al-Ka'bi and al-Jubba'i regarding whether such an action is evidence for knowledge in the unseen, but the core point stands: reason immediately judges that a perfect act implies a knowledgeable agent. The author then applies this principle to human actions. If a human had the power to create his action, he would need to know the details of how it comes from non-existence to existence, its measures, states, and attributes. But we observe that humans are ignorant of these things—they cannot conceive how something emerges from non-existence, nor can they grasp the spatial and temporal details of their actions. For example, when moving a hand through air, the movement occurs across indivisible parts of space and time; the human cannot know the number of air parts or time parts involved. Therefore, he cannot have creative power over the action. The author further notes ignorance regarding good and evil (husn wa qubh): a person may believe his action is good while it is actually evil, showing lack of knowledge of its true moral quality. Since ignorance is established from all these angles, it proves that creative power belongs to God, not humans. The human's power is only over the action in terms of its being movement or stillness, obedience or disobedience—aspects they can know. The author then presents a dilemma to the opponent: either they concede the argument and accept the truth, or they falsely claim that humans have knowledge of these minute details (which is absurd), or they admit ignorance yet still affirm creative power—contradicting the Qur'anic principle that knowledge is a condition for power. Thus, the conclusion is that humans do not create their actions; all creative power belongs to God.

Misconception: One might think that having knowledge of the outward intention or skill is sufficient for creative power.
Correction: Nasafi insists that creative power requires minute, exhaustive knowledge of all causal details (spatial, temporal, moral), which humans lack.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi's proof, why can humans not have creative power over their actions?
A) Because they lack the physical ability to create anything
B) Because they are ignorant of the detailed measures, air parts, and time parts involved in their actions
C) Because God directly creates all human actions without any human involvement
D) Because the Qur'an explicitly says humans have no power at all

Key Takeaway
Humans cannot create their own actions because they are ignorant of the countless details that creative power would require.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the last time you felt proud of an accomplishment. According to this lesson, you are ignorant of how that action actually came into existence. Can you honestly claim any credit for it? How does this reshape your sense of gratitude and humility?
?
The passage says you are ignorant of the true moral quality of your actions—you might think you are right when you are not. Think of a belief or habit you hold that you are certain is good. What if it is actually evil? Are you willing to submit that certainty to God's standard, even if it means admitting ignorance?
?
If you truly believe that God creates all your actions, what changes about how you face a sin you struggle with? Does this lesson remove your excuse for sin, or does it give you hope that God's power is at work even in your failures? How will you respond to your next moment of weakness knowing this?

The Ignorance Argument Against Human Creative Power
Nasafi proves that human ignorance excludes creative power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why, according to Nasafi, humans cannot have creative power over their actions due to their ignorance of the detailed aspects of those actions.

Core Idea
Human ignorance of the details of action proves they cannot be creators.

This passage presents a sophisticated argument from Imam al-Nasafi against the Mu'tazilite claim that humans create their own actions. By examining the limits of human knowledge, Nasafi demonstrates that creative power requires comprehensive awareness that only God possesses. As you read, notice how he systematically builds his case through multiple aspects of ignorance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to get the flow of the argument.
The Arabic uses dense logical terms; the translation clarifies the steps.
2
Identify the aspects of ignorance
Nasafi enumerates several things the human does not know: parts of air/space, number of movements, measure of time, true good/evil. List them as you read.
Each aspect is a separate reason why the human lacks the knowledge needed for creative power.
3
Understand the three options for the opponent
Nasafi presents the Mu'tazilite with three choices: admit the truth, claim knowledge, or affirm power despite ignorance. See how he refutes each.
The third option leads to contradiction with Qur'an and intellect.
4
Grasp the final refutation
Consider the possibility that the action is under no one's power—Nasafi shows this leads to self-causation and denial of the Creator.
This closes every escape route for the opponent.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Summarize the argument: because the condition of detailed knowledge is absent, creative power cannot belong to humans. Write a short summary in your own words.
This reinforces the core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا لم يكن عالما بعدد أجزاء الهواء والمكان لم يكن عالما بعدد الحركات التي حصل فيها الفعل الذي قصد فلم يكن عالما بقدر الفعل وكذا يكون جاهلا بقدر الزمان الذي يشغله بفعله وفي كل جزء لا يتجزأ من الزمان يحصل فعل على حدة، فكان الجهل بأجزاء الزمان جهلا بعدد الافعال التي يحصل بمجموعها ما هو المقصود. وكذا يخرج عن حسن وقبح لا يبلغ علمه قدرهما بل يحصل اعتقاد الكافر والمبتدع على قبح لا علم لهما به البتة بل يظن كل واحد منهما أن اعتقاده في غاية الحسن ونهاية الصحة وهو موصوف بضد ذلك، ولما ثبت جهله بفعله من هذه الوجوه دل أن لا قدرة له عليه من هذه الوجوه، فكان من هذه الوجوه متعلقا بقدرة غيره وهو يعلم به من حيث إنه حركة أو سكونا طاعة أو معصية مأمور به أو منهي عنه، فكان له من هذه الوجوه عليه قدرة فإن ساعدت الخصوم على هذا فقد انقادوا للحق وأبطلوا مذهبهم، وإن ادعوا ثبوت علم للعبد بهذه الوجوه كابروا وعاندوا وادعوا ما يعرفون كذبهم فيه بيقين، وإن سلموا فقد العلم وثبوت الجهل بهذه الوجوه ومع ذلك أثبتوا للعباد قدرة الفعل مع جهلهم بهذه الوجوه فقد ناقضوا وعاندوا كتاب الله تعالى في جعله العلم بذلك شرطا لثبوت القدرة وخرجوا أيضا عن شهادات المعارف، وإن زعموا أن الأفعال من هذه الوجوه ليست بداخله تحت قدرة العبد لانعدام شريطة القدرة وليست بداخله أيضا تحت قدرة الله ولا حاصلة بها، فقد جعلوا حصول الفعل من هذه الوجوه بذاته من غير حاجة إلى مع كونه حدثا، ولو جاز ذا في الفعل لجاز في جميع المعالم، ولو جاز ذا في جميع العالم لبطلت الدلالة على ثبوت الصانع مع أن التكليف بهذا الفعل، والثواب والعقاب عليه لما جاز ولم يقبح مع أنه من هذه الوجوه غير داخل تحت قدرته لماذا لم يجز لو كان الفعل من هذه الوجوه داخلا تحت قدرة الله تعالى؟ فأي فرق في حق العبد بين أن يكون الفعل من هذه الوجوه داخلا تحت قدرة الله تعالى وبين أن لا يكون داخلا تحت قدرة أحد إذا كان خارجا عن قدرته من هذه الوجوه؟ فإذا تقرر بما ذكرنا ما ادعينا من انعدام شريطة ثبوت قدرة التخليق للعبد والله الموفق.
If he is not knowing the number of parts of the air and the place, he is not knowing the number of movements in which occurred the action he intended, so he is not knowing the measure of the action. And likewise he is ignorant of the measure of the time he occupies with his action, and in every indivisible part of time an action occurs separately, so ignorance of the parts of time is ignorance of the number of actions by the totality of which what is intended occurs. And likewise he comes out of [knowledge of] good and evil; his knowledge does not reach their measure. Rather, the belief of the disbeliever and the innovator occurs upon evil while they have no knowledge of it at all, but each of them thinks that his belief is at the extreme of goodness and the utmost correctness, while he is described by the opposite of that. And since his ignorance of his action is established from these aspects, it indicates that he has no power over it from these aspects. So from these aspects it is dependent on the power of another, and he knows it insofar as it is a movement or stillness, an obedience or a disobedience, commanded or forbidden. So from these aspects [the other] has power over it. If the opponents concede this, then they have submitted to the truth and nullified their doctrine. And if they claim the existence of knowledge for the slave concerning these aspects, they are obstinate and stubborn and claim what they know is false with certainty. And if they concede the loss of knowledge and the existence of ignorance concerning these aspects, yet still affirm for the slaves power over the action despite their ignorance of these aspects, then they have contradicted and opposed the Book of Allah Almighty in making knowledge of that a condition for the existence of power, and they have also departed from the testimonies of the intellects. And if they claim that actions from these aspects are not within the power of the slave due to the absence of the condition of power, and are also not within the power of God and not produced by Him, then they have made the occurrence of the action from these aspects come about by itself without need for an agent despite its being a temporal event. And if this were permissible for the action, it would be permissible for all existents. And if this were permissible for all existents, the indication of the existence of the Maker would be nullified, despite the fact that this action is the object of obligation, and reward and punishment are upon it. Since it is, from these aspects, not within his power, why would it not be permissible if the action from these aspects were within the power of God Almighty? What difference is there for the slave between the action being from these aspects within the power of God Almighty and it not being within the power of anyone when it is outside his own power from these aspects? So when what we have claimed regarding the absence of the condition for the existence of creative power for the slave is established by what we have mentioned. And God is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 876

Commentary
This passage is a proof that humans cannot have creative power (qudra takhlīq) over their actions because they lack the detailed knowledge necessary for such power. Nasafi follows a step-by-step argument: he first shows that a human does not know the number of parts of air and space involved in his movement, nor the number of movements, nor the measure of time, nor the precise goodness or evil of his action. Since he is ignorant of these detailed aspects, he cannot have power over the action in its true reality as a created thing. The action, in these detailed aspects, is dependent on the power of another (i.e., God). The opponent (the Mu'tazila) faces three options: 1) admit the truth and abandon their doctrine; 2) claim that the human does have such detailed knowledge, which is false; 3) admit ignorance yet still affirm human power, contradicting the Qur'anic condition that knowledge is a prerequisite for power. Then Nasafi refutes the possibility that the action is not under anyone's power, for that would make it self-caused, leading to the denial of the Creator and the nullification of obligation, reward, and punishment. He concludes that the condition for creative power is absent in humans, so they cannot be creators of their actions.

علم
فعل
شريطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Nasafi denies all human agency, but he only denies creative power (takhliq), not moral responsibility.
Correction: Nasafi affirms that humans have power over actions from a moral perspective (movement/stillness, obedience/disobedience) but denies the detailed creative power that only God possesses.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why can humans not have creative power over their actions?
A) Because they lack the ability to move their limbs.
B) Because they are ignorant of the detailed parts and measures of their actions.
C) Because God directly creates everything without any human involvement.
D) Because actions are not real entities.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi proves that creative power requires knowledge beyond human reach, so only God can be the creator of actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform an action, do you ever pause to consider how many unknowable details (like the parts of air and time) are beyond your awareness? How does this realization change your sense of control over your own deeds? Will you consciously rely more on God's power today, acknowledging your complete dependence on Him for every movement?
?
The passage says that even disbelievers and innovators think their beliefs are the utmost good while they are the opposite. What if some of your deeply held assumptions about your own righteousness or intentions are similarly misguided? Are you willing to submit your self-assessment to God's measure of good and evil, rather than your own? Commit today to asking God to show you the true reality of your actions before you act.
?
Nasafi argues that if you claim to have creative power over your actions, you must either claim knowledge you clearly lack or contradict reason and revelation. In what areas of your life do you subtly—or openly—act as if you are the creator of your own success, morality, or destiny? How will you today actively affirm that God alone is the creator of everything, including your obedience?

Objection and Reply: Possibility of Knowledge
Nasafi answers the objection that humans might know the details of their actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazilite objection that knowledge of actions could be possible for humans, and why the debate centers on actual actions performed in ignorance.

Core Idea
Theoretical possibility does not override the reality of human ignorance in actions.

In this passage, Nasafi addresses a key objection from the Mu'tazila who argue that since it is possible for humans to know the details of their actions, they must also have the power to create them. Nasafi's reply is sharp: the dispute is about actual actions that occur without such knowledge, not hypothetical scenarios. He further argues that even if knowledge were possible, the ability to bring something from non-existence into existence is beyond human capacity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection carefully: the opponent claims that if it is possible for a human to have knowledge of their action's details, then it is also possible for them to have the power to create that action.
Notice how the opponent builds a conditional: if condition (knowledge) is possible, then power is possible.
2
Identify the first reply: diversion
Nasafi calls this objection a 'diversion' (عدول) from the real issue. The dispute is about actual actions that occur while the human is ignorant of the details, not hypothetical cases where knowledge exists.
The key point is that the actions in question are already proven to be impossible for humans to create.
3
Examine the further arguments
Nasafi adds two more points: (1) Humans cannot truly grasp bringing something from non-existence into existence (creative power), so the condition for such power is inconceivable. (2) Even if the condition existed, it does not necessitate the existence of the thing conditioned when the thing itself is impossible.
These arguments reinforce that the objection fails even on its own terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: من الجائزات ثبوت العلم للعبد بفعله من هذه الوجوه، وإذا كان ثبوت الشرط من الجائزات كان ثبوت القدرة من الجائزات. قيل لهم هذا عدول عن الكلام في المتنازع ، فإن المتنازع بيننا وبينكم وقع في هذه الأفعال الحاصلة مع الجهل من العباد بها بهذه الوجوه، فادعيتم أنتم كونها مخلوقة للعباد، ونحن أثبنا ذلك وثبتنا بالدليل استحالته بحمد الله تعالى. فبعد ذلك تصور ثبوت هذه الشريطة في الجملة مما لا ينفعكم، على أنا نقول: ليس في مقدور البشر الاطلاع على الإخراج من العدم إلى الوجود فلا يتصور شريطة قدرة التخليق، على أن ثبوت شريطة الشيء مما لا يوجب ثبوته إذا امتنع
If they say: Among possibilities is the existence of knowledge for the slave concerning his action from these aspects, and if the existence of the condition is among possibilities, then the existence of power is among possibilities. It is said to them: This is a diversion from the speech about the disputed matter. For the dispute between us and you occurred concerning these actions that occur with ignorance of them from these aspects on the part of the slaves. You claimed that they are created by the slaves, and we established that and proved by evidence its impossibility, praise be to God. After that, imagining the existence of this condition in general does not benefit you. Moreover, we say: It is not within the capacity of humans to have access to bringing forth from non-existence to existence, so the condition of creative power is not conceivable. Moreover, the existence of the condition of a thing does not necessitate its existence when it is impossible.
Source pages p. 877

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The opponent (Mu'tazila) objects: 'It is possible for a human to have knowledge of all those detailed aspects of his action, and if the condition (knowledge) is possible, then power is also possible.' Nasafi replies that this is a diversion from the actual disputed issue. The dispute is about real actions that occur while the human is ignorant of these details. The opponent claims these actions are created by humans, but Nasafi has already proven that impossibility. The mere theoretical possibility of knowledge in some cases does not change the fact that for the actions in question, the condition is absent. Furthermore, Nasafi adds that even if knowledge were possible, it is beyond human capacity to truly grasp the act of bringing something from non-existence into existence — that is the condition for creative power (qudra takhlīq), which is inconceivable for humans. Finally, the existence of a condition does not necessarily entail the existence of the thing conditioned, especially when the thing itself is impossible.

Key Terms
جائز
شريطة
متنازع
إخراج من العدم إلى الوجود
قدرة التخليق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection might seem like a fair point, as if possibility of knowledge naturally leads to possibility of power.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that the debate is about actual actions performed in ignorance, not hypothetical ones. Even if knowledge were possible, humans cannot perform the act of bringing from non-existence, and the existence of a condition does not necessitate the existence of the conditioned when the latter is impossible.

Checkpoint
How does Nasafi respond to the objection that knowledge of actions could be possible for humans?
A) He agrees and says power is also possible.
B) He says the objection is a diversion from the actual disputed actions which occur in ignorance.
C) He argues that knowledge is impossible for all actions.
D) He says that even if knowledge is possible, power does not follow.

Key Takeaway
The possibility of knowledge in some hypothetical sense does not prove that humans create their actual actions, especially when those actions occur in ignorance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make a plan and execute it, do you truly know all the hidden details that made it possible? How does your ignorance humble your sense of self-sufficiency? Will you thank Allah more sincerely for every action you complete?
?
Nasafi reminds us that humans cannot bring anything from non-existence. Consider a skill or achievement you are proud of. Where did your ability to do that really come from? Does this truth change the way you view your own efforts? What will you attribute your successes to from now on?
